Automatically classifies tasks into compliance tiers and enforces appropriate verification.\n\n**Key Benefits**:\n- Single command replaces confusion between `sc:task` and `sc:task-mcp`\n- Automatic tier classification with confidence scoring\n- Appropriate verification for each task type\n- Prevents over-engineering for trivial changes\n- Ensures safety for critical changes\n\n## Triggers\n\nUse `/sc:task` when:\n- Task involves code modifications with downstream impacts\n- Complexity score >0.6 with code modifications\n- Multi-file scope (>2 estimated affected files)\n- Security domain paths detected (auth/, security/, crypto/)\n- Refactoring or system-wide changes requested\n\n**Auto-Suggest Keywords**:\n- High confidence: \"implement feature\", \"refactor system\", \"fix security\", \"add authentication\", \"update database schema\"\n- Moderate confidence: \"add new\", \"create component\", \"update service\", \"modify API\"\n\n## Usage\n\n```bash\n/sc:task [description]                           # Auto-detect all dimensions\n/sc:task [description] --compliance strict       # Force STRICT tier\n/sc:task [description] --compliance light        # Force LIGHT tier\n/sc:task [description] --skip-compliance         # Bypass compliance (escape hatch)\n/sc:task [description] --verify auto             # Auto-select verification\n```\n\n## Behavioral Flow\n\n### 0. Activate project (mcp__serena__activate_project)\n2. Verify git working directory clean (git status)\n3. Load codebase context (codebase-retrieval)\n4. Check relevant memories (list_memories -> read_memory)\n5. Identify all affected files and test files\n6. Make changes with full checklist\n7. Identify all files that import changed code\n8. Update all affected files\n9. Spawn verification agent (quality-engineer)\n10. Run comprehensive tests: `pytest [path] -v`\n11. Answer adversarial questions\n\n**STANDARD Execution**:\n1. Load context via codebase-retrieval\n2. Search downstream impacts (find_referencing_symbols OR grep)\n3. Make changes\n4. Run affected tests OR document manual verification\n5. Verify basic functionality\n\n**LIGHT Execution**:\n1. Quick scope check (files/lines within bounds)\n2. Make changes\n3. Quick sanity check (syntax valid, no obvious errors)\n4. Proceed with judgment\n\n**EXEMPT Execution**:\n1. Execute immediately\n2. No verification overhead\n\n### 4. Verification Phase\n\nRoute to appropriate verification based on tier and paths:\n\n| Compliance Tier | Verification Method | Token Cost | Timeout |\n|-----------------|---------------------|------------|---------|\n| STRICT | Sub-agent (quality-engineer) | 3-5K | 60s |\n| STANDARD | Direct test execution | 300-500 | 30s |\n| LIGHT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n| EXEMPT | Skip verification | 0 | 0s |\n\n**Critical Path Override**: Paths matching `auth/`, `security/`, `crypto/`, `models/`, `migrations/` always trigger CRITICAL verification regardless of compliance tier.\n\n**Trivial Path Override**: Paths matching `*.md`, `docs/`, `*test*.py` may skip verification.\n\n### 5. Feedback Collection\n\nAfter completion, collect implicit feedback:\n- Track if user overrode tier (implicit classification feedback)\n- Note smooth completion vs errors (quality signal)\n- Store for calibration learning\n\n## MCP Integration\n\n**Required Servers by Tier**:\n- STRICT: Sequential, Serena (fallback not allowed)\n- STANDARD: Sequential, Context7 (fallback allowed)\n- LIGHT: None required (fallback allowed)\n- EXEMPT: None required\n\n**Circuit Breaker Behavior**:\n- If required servers unavailable for STRICT tier, block task execution\n- For other tiers, use fallbacks with noted limitations\n\n## Tool Coordination\n\n**Planning Phase**:\n1. TodoWrite: Create task breakdown\n2. codebase-retrieval: Load context\n3. list_memories / read_memory: Check project state\n\n**Execution Phase**:\n1. Edit/MultiEdit/Write: Make changes\n2. Grep/Glob: Find references\n3. find_referencing_symbols: Trace dependencies\n\n**Verification Phase**:\n1. Task (quality-engineer): Spawn verification agent (STRICT only)\n2. Bash: Run tests directly (STANDARD)\n3. think_about_task_adherence: Reflect on completeness\n\n**Completion Phase**:\n1. write_memory: Save session state\n2. think_about_whether_you_are_done: Final {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_wIreqFueyeXbmp959VxhuMUt","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# D-0010: Contract Schema Versioning Policy\n     2→\n     3→**Task**: T02.01\n     4→**Roadmap Items**: R-018, R-019, R-020, R-026\n     5→**Date**: 2026-03-08\n     6→\n     7→## Schema Version Format\n     8→\n     9→All portify contracts use semantic versioning in the `schema_version` field:\n    10→\n    11→```\n    12→schema_version: \"1.0\"\n    13→```\n    14→\n    15→**Format**: `MAJOR.MINOR` (string, quoted)\n    16→- **MAJOR**: Incremented on breaking changes (field removal, type change, semantic redefinition)\n    17→- **MINOR**: Incremented on additive changes (new optional fields)\n    18→\n    19→## Backward-Compatibility Rules\n    20→\n    21→| Change Type | Allowed? | Version Impact |\n    22→|-------------|----------|----------------|\n    23→| Add new optional field | Yes | Minor bump |\n    24→| Add new required field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    25→| Remove field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    26→| Change field type | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    27→| Change allowed enum values (additive) | Yes | Minor bump |\n    28→| Remove enum value | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    29→| Rename field | No (breaking) | Major bump |\n    30→\n    31→## Version Validation on Contract Read\n    32→\n    33→When a phase reads an incoming contract:\n    34→\n    35→1. Parse `schema_version` field\n    36→2. Extract `MAJOR.MINOR` components\n    37→3. Validate compatibility:\n    38→   - **Same MAJOR, same or lower MINOR**: Compatible — proceed\n    39→   - **Higher MINOR**: Compatible (additive fields ignored by older consumer) — proceed with advisory warning\n    40→   - **Different MAJOR**: Incompatible — abort with actionable error\n    41→\n    42→**Error format on incompatible version**:\n    43→\n    44→```\n    45→CONTRACT_VERSION_MISMATCH: Expected schema_version 1.x, got 2.0.\n    46→Phase {N} contract at {path} was produced by an incompatible schema version.\n    47→Action: Re-run Phase {N-1} to regenerate the contract with schema version 1.x.\n    48→```\n    49→\n    50→## Common Header Schema\n    51→\n    52→Every portify contract includes this common header:\n    53→\n    54→```yaml\n    55→schema_version: \"1.0\"          # String. Required. Format: \"MAJOR.MINOR\"\n    56→phase: <int>                    # Integer 0-4. Required. Producing phase number.\n    57→status: <enum>                  # String. Required. One of: \"passed\", \"failed\", \"skipped\"\n    58→timestamp: <ISO8601>            # String. Required. UTC ISO 8601 datetime.\n    59→resume_checkpoint: <string>     # String. Required. Identifier for resume point.\n    60→                                # Format: \"phase-{N}:{step}\" e.g. \"phase-0:collision-check\"\n    61→validation_status:              # Object. Required.\n    62→  blocking_passed: <int>        # Integer. Count of blocking validations that passed.\n    63→  blocking_failed: <int>        # Integer. Count of blocking validations that failed.\n    64→  advisory: <list[string]>      # List of strings. Advisory warnings (non-blocking).\n    65→```\n    66→\n    67→**Field Type Summary**:\n    68→\n    69→| Field | Type | Required | Allowed Values |\n    70→|-------|------|----------|----------------|\n    71→| `schema_version` | string | Yes | Semantic version \"MAJOR.MINOR\" |\n    72→| `phase` | integer | Yes | 0, 1, 2, 3, 4 |\n    73→| `status` | string | Yes | \"passed\", \"failed\", \"skipped\" |\n    74→| `timestamp` | string | Yes | ISO 8601 UTC datetime |\n    75→| `resume_checkpoint` | string | Yes | \"phase-{N}:{step}\" |\n    76→| `validation_status` | object | Yes | See sub-fields |\n    77→| `validation_status.blocking_passed` | integer | Yes | >= 0 |\n    78→| `validation_status.blocking_failed` | integer | Yes | >= 0 |\n    79→| `validation_status.advisory` | list[string] | Yes | Free-form advisory messages |\n    80→\n    81→## Null-Field Policy\n    82→\n    83→Fields for unreached phases or inapplicable data are explicitly set to `null`, never omitted.\n    84→\n    85→**Rules**:\n    86→1. All fields defined in a contract schema MUST be present in the emitted YAML\n    87→2. Unreached or inapplicable fields are set to `null`\n    88→3. Empty lists are represented as `[]`, not `null`\n    89→4. Empty objects are represented as `{}`, not `null`\n    90→5. A consumer reading a contract can distinguish \"not yet computed\" (`null`) from \"computed and empty\" (`[]` / `{}`)\n    91→\n    92→**Example — Phase 0 contract emitted before Phase 1 runs**:\n    93→\n    94→```yaml\n    95→schema_version: \"1.0\"\n    96→phase: 0\n    97→status: \"passed\"\n    98→timestamp: \"2026-03-08T14:30:00Z\"\n    99→resume_checkpoint: \"phase-0:complete\"\n   100→validation_status:\n   101→  blocking_passed: 3\n   102→  blocking_failed: 0\n   103→  advisory: []\n   104→# Phase 0 specific fields populated:\n   105→workflow_path: \"src/superclaude/skills/sc-cleanup-audit-protocol/\"\n   106→api_snapshot_hash: \"sha256:abc123...\"\n   107→collision_status: \"clean\"\n   108→pattern_scan_result: \"supported\"\n   109→# Phase 1+ fields not yet populated:\n   110→component_inventory: null\n   111→step_graph: null\n   112→```\n   113→\n   114→## Contract File Naming Convention\n   115→\n   116→| Phase | Contract File | Producer | Consumer |\n   117→|-------|--------------|----------|----------|\n   118→| 0 | `portify-prerequisites.yaml` | Phase 0 | Phase 1 |\n   119→| 1 | `portify-analysis.yaml` | Phase 1 | Phase 2 |\n   120→| 2 | `portify-spec.yaml` | Phase 2 | Phase 3 |\n   121→| 3 | `portify-codegen.yaml` | Phase 3 | Phase 4 |\n   122→| 4 | `portify-integration.yaml` | Phase 4 | Return contract |\n   123→| Return | embedded in return contract | Phase 5 / aggregator | Caller |\n   124→\n   125→## Schema Version History\n   126→\n   127→| Version | Date | Changes |\n   128→|---------|------|---------|\n   129→| {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_CjLJxy7MwxpkQZcrdo1hjwRF","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# D-0012: Contract Validation and Resume Protocol Specification\n     2→\n     3→**Task**: T02.03\n     4→**Roadmap Items**: R-022, R-023, R-024, R-025\n     5→**Date**: 2026-03-08\n     6→**Depends On**: D-0010 (versioning policy), D-0011 (per-phase schemas)\n     7→\n     8→---\n     9→\n    10→## 1. Contract Validation Logic\n    11→\n    12→### Interface\n    13→\n    14→```\n    15→validate_contract(contract_path: str, expected_phase: int) -> ValidatedContract | ContractError\n    16→```\n    17→\n    18→### Validation Steps\n    19→\n    20→On reading an incoming contract, the validator performs these checks in order:\n    21→\n    22→#### Step 1: File Existence and Parse\n    23→- Verify file exists at `contract_path`\n    24→- Parse YAML content\n    25→- On parse failure: return `ContractError(\"YAML_PARSE_FAILED\", path, details)`\n    26→\n    27→#### Step 2: Common Header Validation\n    28→- Verify `schema_version` field exists and is a string matching `\"MAJOR.MINOR\"` pattern\n    29→- Verify `phase` field exists and equals `expected_phase - 1` (the producing phase)\n    30→- Verify `status` field exists and is one of: `\"passed\"`, `\"failed\"`, `\"skipped\"`\n    31→- Verify `timestamp` field exists and is a valid ISO 8601 string\n    32→- Verify `resume_checkpoint` field exists and is a non-empty string\n    33→- Verify `validation_status` object exists with `blocking_passed`, `blocking_failed`, `advisory` sub-fields\n    34→\n    35→#### Step 3: Schema Version Compatibility\n    36→- Parse `schema_version` into MAJOR and MINOR integers\n    37→- Compare against expected version (currently \"1.0\"):\n    38→  - Same MAJOR, any MINOR: **compatible** (proceed)\n    39→  - Different MAJOR: **incompatible** (abort)\n    40→- On incompatible version:\n    41→  ```\n    42→  ContractError(\n    43→    code=\"CONTRACT_VERSION_MISMATCH\",\n    44→    message=\"Expected schema_version 1.x, got {actual}. \"\n    45→            \"Phase {expected_phase - 1} contract at {path} was produced by an incompatible schema version. \"\n    46→            \"Action: Re-run Phase {expected_phase - 1} to regenerate the contract with schema version 1.x.\"\n    47→  )\n    48→  ```\n    49→\n    50→#### Step 4: Required Field Presence (Phase-Specific)\n    51→- Load the expected field set for the contract's phase from the schema registry (D-0011)\n    52→- For each required field:\n    53→  - Verify field key exists in parsed YAML\n    54→  - `null` values are allowed (per null-field policy from D-0010)\n    55→  - Missing keys are NOT allowed\n    56→- On missing required fields:\n    57→  ```\n    58→  ContractError(\n    59→    code=\"MISSING_REQUIRED_FIELDS\",\n    60→    message=\"Contract at {path} is missing required fields: {missing_fields}. \"\n    61→            \"Action: Re-run Phase {phase} to regenerate the contract.\"\n    62→  )\n    63→  ```\n    64→\n    65→#### Step 5: Status Enum Validation\n    66→- Verify `status` is one of the allowed values: `\"passed\"`, `\"failed\"`, `\"skipped\"`\n    67→- Verify `phase` is in range 0-4 (or -1 for return contract)\n    68→\n    69→#### Step 6: Blocking Failure Check\n    70→- If `status == \"failed\"` AND `validation_status.blocking_failed > 0`:\n    71→  - Return validated contract with `can_proceed = False`\n    72→  - Include failure details for downstream decision-making\n    73→\n    74→### Output\n    75→\n    76→```\n    77→ValidatedContract:\n    78→  data: dict              # Parsed and validated contract data\n    79→  schema_version: str     # Parsed version\n    80→  phase: int              # Producing phase\n    81→  status: str             # \"passed\" | \"failed\" | \"skipped\"\n    82→  can_proceed: bool       # True if consuming phase should proceed\n    83→  warnings: list[str]     # Advisory warnings (e.g., higher minor version)\n    84→```\n    85→\n    86→---\n    87→\n    88→## 2. Return Contract Assembly\n    89→\n    90→### Interface\n    91→\n    92→```\n    93→assemble_return_contract(phase_contracts: dict[int, ValidatedContract], pipeline_state: PipelineState) -> dict\n    94→```\n    95→\n    96→### Assembly Logic\n    97→\n    98→1. **Determine overall status**:\n    99→   - If all phases passed: `status = \"passed\"`\n   100→   - If any phase failed: `status = \"failed\"`\n   101→   - If pipeline was halted before completion: `status = \"failed\"`\n   102→\n   103→2. **Identify failure information**:\n   104→   - `failure_phase`: Phase number where first failure occurred, `null` if passed\n   105→   - `failure_type`: Classification of failure, `null` if passed\n   106→     - `\"validation_failed\"`: Self-validation check failed\n   107→     - `\"gate_failed\"`: Gate validation failed\n   108→     - `\"unsupported_pattern\"`: Phase 0 detected unsupported pattern\n   109→     - `\"collision\"`: Output directory collision detected\n   110→     - `\"generation_error\"`: Code generation failed\n   111→     - `\"integration_error\"`: main.py patching or smoke test failed\n   112→\n   113→3. **Aggregate generated files**:\n   114→   - Collect all file paths from Phase 3 `generated_files` and Phase 4 outputs\n   115→   - Include `portify-analysis.md`, `portify-spec.md`, `portify-summary.md` if they exist\n   116→\n   117→4. **Compute counts**:\n   118→   - `total_steps`: From Phase 1 `step_graph` length\n   119→   - `programmatic_steps`: Count where `classification == \"pure_programmatic\"`\n   120→   - `claude_assisted_steps`: Count where `classification == \"claude_assisted\"`\n   121→   - `hybrid_steps`: Count where `classification == \"hybrid\"`\n   122→   - `files_generated`: From Phase 3 `generated_files` length\n   123→   - `gates_passed` / `gates_failed`: From Phase 3 validation results\n   124→\n   125→5. **Populate remaining fields**:\n   126→   - `api_snapshot_hash`: From Phase 0 `api_snapshot.content_hash`\n   127→   - `resume_command`: Generated from failure point if failed, `null` if passed\n   128→   - `warnings`: Aggregated from all `validation_status.advisory` lists\n   129→   - `phase_contracts`: Embed each phase contract (or `null` if phase not reached)\n   130→\n   131→6. **Apply null-field policy**: Any field not computable (because a phase wasn't reached) is set to `null`\n   132→\n   133→### Return Contract Emission\n   134→\n   135→The return contract is ALWAYS emitted, even on failure. This ensures:\n   136→- Callers always get structured output\n   137→- Resume information is always available\n   138→- Partial results are preserved\n   139→\n   140→---\n   141→\n   142→## 3. Resume Protocol\n   143→\n   144→### Interface\n   145→\n   146→```\n   147→resume_pipeline(resume_checkpoint: str, contract_dir: str) -> ResumeResult\n   148→```\n   149→\n   150→### Resume Flow\n   151→\n   152→#### Step 1: Read Latest Contract State\n   153→- Scan `contract_dir` for all `portify-*.yaml` files\n   154→- Parse each contract and build phase completion map:\n   155→  ```\n   156→  phase_state = {\n   157→    0: ValidatedContract | None,\n   158→    1: ValidatedContract | None,\n   159→    2: ValidatedContract | None,\n   160→    3: ValidatedContract | None,\n   161→    4: ValidatedContract | None,\n   162→  }\n   163→  ```\n   164→\n   165→#### Step 2: Parse Resume Checkpoint\n   166→- Parse `resume_checkpoint` format: `\"phase-{N}:{step}\"`\n   167→- Extract target phase number and step within that phase\n   168→- Validate: target phase must be >= 0 and <= 4\n   169→\n   170→#### Step 3: Validate Completed Phase Contracts\n   171→- For each phase BEFORE the target phase (phase < target):\n   172→  - If contract exists: re-validate using `validate_contract()`\n   173→  - If contract is missing: error — cannot resume without prior phase output\n   174→  - If contract fails re-validation: error — prior phase output is corrupt\n   175→  - **Contracts are NOT blindly trusted on resume** — they are re-validated\n   176→\n   177→#### Step 4: Determine Resume Entry Point\n   178→- Skip all phases with `status == \"passed\"` AND valid contracts\n   179→- Resume at `target_phase` from the specified step\n   180→- If the target phase's contract exists with `status == \"failed\"`:\n   181→  - Re-execute from the beginning of that phase (not the failed step within it)\n   182→  - Rationale: partial phase state may be inconsistent\n   183→\n   184→#### Step 5: Verify Filesystem Consistency\n   185→- If Phase 0 contract exists, verify `api_snapshot.content_hash` still matches the live snapshot\n   186→- If hash mismatch: warn that API may have changed since original run\n   187→  - Advisory warning, not blocking (user may have intentionally updated API)\n   188→\n   189→### Output\n   190→\n   191→```\n   192→ResumeResult:\n   193→  resume_from_phase: int           # Phase to resume from\n   194→  validated_prior_contracts: dict   # Re-validated prior phase contracts\n   195→  warnings: list[str]             # Advisory warnings (e.g., API hash mismatch)\n   196→  can_resume: bool                # True if resume is possible\n   197→  error: str | None               # Error message if resume is not possible\n   198→```\n   199→\n   200→### Resume Error Cases\n   201→\n   202→| Error | Cause | Action |\n   203→|-------|-------|--------|\n   204→| `NO_CONTRACTS_FOUND` | No portify-*.yaml in contract_dir | Start from Phase 0 |\n   205→| `PRIOR_CONTRACT_MISSING` | Phase N-1 contract missing | Re-run from Phase N-1 |\n   206→| `PRIOR_CONTRACT_CORRUPT` | Phase N-1 contract fails re-validation | Re-run from Phase N-1 |\n   207→| `INVALID_CHECKPOINT` | resume_checkpoint format invalid | Report error |\n   208→| `PHASE_OUT_OF_RANGE` | Target phase > 4 or < 0 | Report error |\n   209→\n   210→---\n   211→\n   212→## 4. Contract Error Codes\n   213→\n   214→| Code | Meaning | Severity |\n   215→|------|---------|----------|\n   216→| `YAML_PARSE_FAILED` | Contract file is not valid YAML | Blocking |\n   217→| `CONTRACT_VERSION_MISMATCH` | Major version incompatible | Blocking |\n   218→| `MISSING_REQUIRED_FIELDS` | Required fields absent from contract | Blocking |\n   219→| `INVALID_STATUS_ENUM` | Status field has invalid value | Blocking |\n   220→| `INVALID_PHASE_NUMBER` | Phase number out of range | Blocking |\n   221→| `PRIOR_CONTRACT_MISSING` | Resume needs prior contract that doesn't exist | Blocking |\n   222→| `PRIOR_CONTRACT_CORRUPT` | Prior contract fails re-validation | Blocking |\n   223→| `API_HASH_MISMATCH` | API snapshot hash changed since original run | Advisory |\n   224→| `HIGHER_MINOR_VERSION` | Contract has higher minor version than expected | Advisory |\n   225→"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_0171Sc4TRdF2QGEGsu6am8qF","session_id":"392951ff-641a-4718-a34a-e7e268437669","uuid":"b522c65c-aa65-4a1c-933a-a329b0a2c477"}

Step Decomposition Engine (FR-016, FR-049)\n    54→\n    55→### ID Assignment Algorithm\n    56→\n    57→```\n    58→decompose_steps(skill_md: str, analysis_protocol: str) -> list[SourceStep]\n    59→```\n    60→\n    61→Steps are identified by applying the boundary detection rules from `refs/analysis-protocol.md`:\n    62→\n    63→**A new Step starts when**:\n    64→- A new artifact is produced\n    65→- A different agent takes over\n    66→- The execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n    67→- A quality gate must be evaluated\n    68→- The operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n    69→\n    70→Steps are assigned stable `source_id` values in format `S-NNN`:\n    71→\n    72→1. **Ordering**: Steps are numbered in the order they appear in the workflow's behavioral flow\n    73→2. **Stability**: Same workflow text always produces same step boundaries and IDs\n    74→3. **Conservation Invariant**: `|source_steps| == |classified_steps|`\n    75→   - Every identified step MUST receive exactly one classification\n    76→   - No steps may be added or removed during classification\n    77→   - This invariant is checked after classification and recorded in the contract\n    78→\n    79→### Conservation Invariant Enforcement\n    80→\n    81→```\n    82→enforce_conservation(source_steps: list, classified_steps: list) -> ConservationResult\n    83→```\n    84→\n    85→```yaml\n    86→conservation_invariant:\n    87→  source_step_count: N       # Number of steps identified by decomposition\n    88→  classified_step_count: N   # Number of steps after classification\n    89→  invariant_holds: true      # source_step_count == classified_step_count\n    90→```\n    91→\n    92→If invariant fails: **blocking error** — classification modified the step list. This is a bug in the classification engine.\n    93→\n    94→### Test Execution: sc-cleanup-audit-protocol\n    95→\n    96→The cleanup-audit workflow has a multi-pass audit structure (pattern from analysis-protocol.md):\n    97→\n    98→| source_id | Name | Boundary Trigger |\n    99→|-----------|------|-----------------|\n   100→| S-001 | Discover and classify files | New artifact (file inventory) |\n   101→| S-002 | Surface scan (Pass 1) — batch | Agent change (audit-scanner) + parallel |\n   102→| S-003 | Structural analysis (Pass 2) — batch | Agent change (audit-analyzer) |\n   103→| S-004 | Cross-cutting comparison (Pass 3) | Agent change (audit-comparator) + mode change |\n   104→| S-005 | Consolidate findings | Agent change (audit-consolidator) |\n   105→| S-006 | Validate claims (spot-check) | Agent change (audit-validator) |\n   106→\n   107→**source_step_count**: 6\n   108→**classified_step_count**: 6\n   109→**Conservation invariant**: `6 == 6` → HOLDS ✅\n   110→\n   111→---\n   112→\n   113→## 3. Step Classification Engine (FR-017)\n   114→\n   115→### Classification Algorithm\n   116→\n   117→```\n   118→classify_steps(source_steps: list[SourceStep]) -> list[ClassifiedStep]\n   119→```\n   120→\n   121→Each step is classified as `pure_programmatic`, `claude_assisted`, or `hybrid` with a confidence score:\n   122→\n   123→| Classification | Criteria | Confidence Factors |\n   124→|---------------|---------|-------------------|\n   125→| `pure_programmatic` | Deterministic, formula-based, structural; uses only Python/bash tools; no natural language judgment | High (0.9+): file listing, math, regex |\n   126→| `claude_assisted` | Content generation, analysis, judgment; requires reading/synthesizing text | High (0.9+): writing reports, rubric evaluation |\n   127→| `hybrid` | Programmatic setup → Claude execution → programmatic validation | Medium (0.7-0.9): structured analysis with validation |\n   128→\n   129→**Confidence scoring factors**:\n   130→- Tool list analysis: if step only uses Read/Grep/Glob/Bash → +0.2 toward programmatic\n   131→- Output analysis: if output is markdown report → +0.2 toward claude_assisted\n   132→- Agent delegation: if step delegates to a Claude agent → +0.3 toward claude_assisted\n   133→- Structural validation: if step has strict gate with semantic checks → +0.1 toward hybrid\n   134→- Determinism: if step could produce different outputs for same input → +0.2 toward claude_assisted\n   135→\n   136→**User review flag**: Steps with confidence < 0.7 are flagged for user review before Phase 2 proceeds.\n   137→\n   138→### Test Execution: sc-cleanup-audit-protocol\n   139→\n   140→| source_id | Name | Classification | Confidence | Flagged? Dependency DAG Builder (FR-018)\n    11→\n    12→### Construction Algorithm\n    13→\n    14→```\n    15→build_dependency_dag(steps: list[ClassifiedStep]) -> DependencyDAG\n    16→```\n    17→\n    18→1. **Node creation**: Each step `S-NNN` becomes a node\n    19→2. **Edge inference**: For each step, examine its `inputs` list:\n    20→   - If step B lists an artifact produced by step A in its inputs → edge A → B\n    21→   - If step B references a `source_id` of step A → edge A → B\n    22→3. **Parallel group handling**: Steps in the same parallel group have no edges between them (independence requirement)\n    23→4. **Implicit ordering**: Steps appearing sequentially in the workflow that share no explicit data dependency are NOT connected (they may run in parallel if classified as independent)\n    24→\n    25→### Acyclicity Validation\n    26→\n    27→```\n    28→validate_acyclicity(dag: DependencyDAG) -> AcyclicityResult\n    29→```\n    30→\n    31→Uses **topological sort** (Kahn's algorithm):\n    32→1. Process queue: dequeue node, reduce in-degrees of successors, enqueue newly zero-degree nodes\n    35→4. If all nodes processed: **acyclic** ✅\n    36→5. IDs are assigned by position in the sorted list, zero-padded to 3 digits.\n\n3. **Output**: Each component record:\n   ```yaml\n   component_id: \"C-001\"\n   path: \"src/superclaude/commands/cleanup-audit.md\"\n   type: \"command\"\n   line_count: 45\n   purpose: \"Slash command entry point for cleanup audit\"\n   ```\n\n### Test Execution: sc-cleanup-audit-protocol\n\n| component_id | Path | Type | Lines | Purpose |\n|-------------|------|------|-------|---------|\n| C-001 | `commands/cleanup-audit.md` | command | ~45 | Command entry point |\n| C-002 | `skills/sc-cleanup-audit-protocol/SKILL.md` | skill | ~800 | Full protocol |\n| C-003 | `skills/sc-cleanup-audit-protocol/refs/...` | ref | varies | Reference files |\n| ... | (sorted alphabetically) | ... | ... | ... |\n\n**Result**: All components assigned unique C-NNN IDs ✅\n\n---\n\n## 2. Step Decomposition Engine (FR-016, FR-049)\n\n### ID Assignment Algorithm\n\n```\ndecompose_steps(skill_md: str, analysis_protocol: str) -> list[SourceStep]\n```\n\nSteps are identified by applying the boundary detection rules from `refs/analysis-protocol.md`:\n\n**A new Step starts when**:\n- A new artifact is produced\n- A different agent takes over\n- The execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n- A quality gate must be evaluated\n- The operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n\nSteps are assigned stable `source_id` values in format `S-NNN`:\n\n1. **Ordering**: Steps are numbered in the order they appear in the workflow's behavioral flow\n2. **Stability**: Same workflow text always produces same step boundaries and IDs\n3. **Conservation Invariant**: `|source_steps| == |classified_steps|`\n   - Every identified step MUST receive exactly one classification\n   - No steps may be added or removed during classification\n   - This invariant is checked after classification and recorded in the contract\n\n### Conservation Invariant Enforcement\n\n```\nenforce_conservation(source_steps: list, classified_steps: list) -> ConservationResult\n```\n\n```yaml\nconservation_invariant:\n  source_step_count: N       # Number of steps identified by decomposition\n  classified_step_count: N   # Number of steps after classification\n  invariant_holds: true      # source_step_count == classified_step_count\n```\n\nIf invariant fails: **blocking error** — classification modified the step list. This is a bug in the classification engine.\n\n### Test Execution: sc-cleanup-audit-protocol\n\nThe cleanup-audit workflow has a multi-pass audit structure (pattern from analysis-protocol.md):\n\n| source_id | Name | Boundary Trigger |\n|-----------|------|-----------------|\n| S-001 | Discover and classify files | New artifact (file inventory) |\n| S-002 | Surface scan (Pass 1) — batch | Agent change (audit-scanner) + parallel |\n| S-003 | Structural analysis (Pass 2) — batch | Agent change (audit-analyzer) |\n| S-004 | Cross-cutting comparison (Pass 3) | Agent change (audit-comparator) + mode change |\n| S-005 | Consolidate findings | Agent change (audit-consolidator) |\n| S-006 | Validate claims (spot-check) | Agent change (audit-validator) |\n\n**source_step_count**: 6\n**classified_step_count**: 6\n**Conservation invariant**: `6 == 6` → HOLDS ✅\n\n---\n\n## 3. Step Classification Engine (FR-017)\n\n### Classification Algorithm\n\n```\nclassify_steps(source_steps: list[SourceStep]) -> list[ClassifiedStep]\n```\n\nEach step is classified as `pure_programmatic`, `claude_assisted`, or `hybrid` with a confidence score:\n\n| Classification | Criteria | Confidence Factors |\n|---------------|---------|-------------------|\n| `pure_programmatic` | Deterministic, formula-based, structural; uses only Python/bash tools; no natural language judgment | High (0.9+): file listing, math, regex |\n| `claude_assisted` | Content generation, analysis, judgment; requires reading/synthesizing text | High (0.9+): writing reports, rubric evaluation |\n| `hybrid` | Programmatic setup → Claude execution → programmatic validation | Medium (0.7-0.9): structured analysis with validation |\n\n**Confidence scoring factors**:\n- Tool list analysis: if step only uses Read/Grep/Glob/Bash → +0.2 toward programmatic\n- Output analysis: if output is markdown report → +0.2 toward claude_assisted\n- Agent delegation: if step delegates to a Claude agent → +0.3 toward claude_assisted\n- Structural validation: if step has strict gate with semantic checks → +0.1 toward hybrid\n- Determinism: if step could produce different outputs for same input → +0.2 toward claude_assisted\n\n**User review flag**: Steps with confidence < 0.7 are flagged for user review before Phase 2 proceeds.\n\n### Test Execution: sc-cleanup-audit-protocol\n\n| source_id | Name | Classification | Confidence | Flagged? |\n|-----------|------|---------------|------------|----------|\n| S-001 | Discover and classify files | `pure_programmatic` | 0.95 | No |\n| S-002 | Surface scan (Pass 1) | `claude_assisted` | 0.90 | No |\n| S-003 | Structural analysis (Pass 2) | `claude_assisted` | 0.90 | No |\n| S-004 | Cross-cutting comparison | `claude_assisted` | 0.85 | No |\n| S-005 | Consolidate findings | `claude_assisted` | 0.88 | No |\n| S-006 | Validate claims (spot-check) | `claude_assisted` | 0.85 | No |\n\n**Classification summary**:\n- Pure programmatic: 1 step (S-001)\n- Claude-assisted: 5 steps (S-002 through S-006)\n- Hybrid: 0 steps\n- Flagged for review: 0 steps (all confidence ≥ 0.7)\n\n---\n\n## 4. Guides the systematic decomposition of an inference-based workflow into a pipeline specification.\n\n## Discovery Checklist\n\nWhen analyzing a target workflow, locate and read these components in order:\n\n### 1. Find the Command\n\nLook in `src/superclaude/commands/` for the matching command file. Extract:\n- Frontmatter: category, complexity, mcp-servers, personas\n- Behavioral Flow section: the high-level step sequence\n- Arguments and options\n- Boundaries (Will Do / Will Not Do)\n\n### 2. Find the Skill\n\nLook in `src/superclaude/skills/` for the matching skill directory. Read:\n- `SKILL.md`: The full protocol with step-by-step behavioral flow\n- `refs/`: All reference files (algorithms, templates, scoring protocols)\n- `rules/`: Validation rules and classification taxonomies\n- `templates/`: Output format templates (these become gate validation targets)\n- `scripts/`: Shell scripts for preprocessing (these become pure-programmatic steps)\n- Note which refs are loaded at which phase/wave\n\n### 3. Find the Agents\n\nSearch for agents referenced in the skill:\n- Look in `src/superclaude/agents/` for `.md` files\n- Note each agent's: triggers, tools, responsibilities, boundaries\n- Identify delegation patterns: parallel vs sequential, orchestrator vs worker\n\n### 4. Map the Data Flow\n\nTrace how data moves through the workflow:\n- What inputs does each step consume?\n- What artifacts does each step produce?\n- Which artifacts feed into downstream steps?\n- What is the final output?\n\n## Step Decomposition Algorithm\n\nFor each discrete operation in the workflow:\n\n### Identify Step Boundaries\n\nA new Step starts when:\n- A new artifact is produced\n- A different agent takes over\n- The execution mode changes (sequential → parallel)\n- A quality gate must be evaluated\n- The operation type changes (analysis → generation → validation)\n\n### Classify Each Step\n\nRate each step on the **programmatic spectrum**:\n\n| Classification | Characteristics | Implementation |\n|---------------|-----------------|----------------|\n| **Pure Programmatic** | Deterministic, formula-based, structural | Python function, no Claude |\n| **Programmatic + Validation** | Structural check with semantic judgment | Python primary, Claude for edge cases |\n| **Claude-Assisted** | Content generation within structured format | Claude subprocess with gate validation |\n| **Pure Inference** | Creative, subjective, context-dependent | Claude subprocess with light gate |\n\n### Map to Pipeline Primitives\n\n| Workflow Concept | Pipeline Primitive |\n|-----------------|-------------------|\n| Sequential step | `Step` in step list |\n| Parallel operations | `list[Step]` parallel group |\n| Quality gate | `GateCriteria` on the Step |\n| Agent delegation | Prompt in `prompts.py` |\n| Scoring formula | Python function in `gates.py` or separate module |\n| Status decision | `_determine_status()` in `executor.py` |\n| Input validation | `config.py` validation logic |\n| Output format | Frontmatter requirements in gate + prompt |\n| Retry on failure | `retry_limit` on Step |\n| Skip on success | Resume logic in executor |\n\n## Analysis Output Format\n\nPhase 1 produces `portify-analysis.md` with this structure:\n\n```markdown\n---\nsource_skill: <skill-name>\nsource_command: <command-name>\nstep_count: <N>\nparallel_groups: <N>\ngate_count: <N>\nagent_count: <N>\ncomplexity: simple|moderate|high\n---\n\n# Portification Analysis: {workflow-name}\n\n## Source Components\n\n| Component | Path | Lines | Purpose |\n|-----------|------|-------|---------|\n| Command | ... | ... | ... |\n| Skill | ... | ... | ... |\n| Agent: ... | ... | ... | ... |\n| Ref: ... | ... | ... | ... |\n\n## Step Graph\n\n### Step 1: {name}\n- **Type**: pure-programmatic | claude-assisted | hybrid\n- **Inputs**: [list of input artifacts]\n- **Output**: artifact-name.md\n- **Gate**: exempt | light | standard | strict\n- **Agent**: none | agent-name\n- **Parallel**: yes (with step N) | no\n- **Timeout**: Ns\n- **Retry**: N attempts\n- **Notes**: any special considerations\n\n### Step 2: {name}\n...\n\n## Parallel Groups\n\n| Group | Steps | Rationale |\n|-------|-------|-----------|\n| 1 | step-2, step-3 | Independent variant generation |\n\n## Gates Summary\n\n| Step | Tier | Frontmatter | Min Lines | Semantic Checks |\n|------|------|-------------|-----------|-----------------|\n| ... | ... | ... | ... | ... |\n\n## Agent Delegation Map\n\n| Agent | Used In Steps | Parallel | Contract |\n|-------|--------------|----------|----------|\n| ... | ... | ... | ... |\n\n## Data Flow Diagram\n\n```\n[input] → step-1 → [artifact-1]\n                         ↓\n                    ┌─step-2─┐\n                    │         │ (parallel)\n                    └─step-3─┘\n                         ↓\n               [artifact-2, artifact-3]\n                         ↓\n                    step-4 → [final-output]\n```\n\n## Classification Summary\n\n| Category | Count | Steps |\n|----------|-------|-------|\n| Pure Programmatic | N | ... |\n| Claude-Assisted | N | ... |\n| Hybrid | N | ... |\n| Pure Inference | N | ... |\n\n## Recommendations\n\n- Things that should definitely be programmatic but are currently inference\n- Steps that could be split for better gate coverage\n- Opportunities for parallelization\n- Potential failure modes and how to handle them\n```\n\n## Common Workflow Patterns\n\n### Pattern: Multi-Agent Debate\nFound in: adversarial, spec-panel\n\nSteps:\n1. Parse inputs and validate (programmatic)\n2. Generate variants in parallel (Claude, parallel group)\n3. Diff analysis (Claude, single step with strict gate)\n4. Debate rounds (Claude, sequential with convergence gate)\n5. Score and select (hybrid — formulas are programmatic, rubrics are Claude)\n6. Generate plan (Claude, standard gate)\n7. Execute merge (Claude, strict gate with post-validation)\n\n### Pattern: Multi-Pass Audit\nFound in: cleanup-audit\n\nSteps:\n1. Discover files (programmatic)\n2. Surface scan with batching (Claude, batched parallel)\n3. Deep analysis per file (Claude, batched parallel)\n4. Cross-cutting comparison (Claude, single with strict gate)\n5. Consolidate findings (Claude, standard gate)\n6. Validate claims (Claude, sampling with standard gate)\n\n### Pattern: Extract-Transform-Validate\nFound in: roadmap, tasklist\n\nSteps:\n1. Extract requirements (Claude, strict gate on frontmatter)\n2. Generate artifacts (Claude, parallel for multiple agents)\n3. Compare/analyze (Claude, standard gate)\n4. Synthesize final (Claude, strict gate)\n5. Validate structure (programmatic)\n\n### Pattern: Iterative Refinement\nFound in: implement, improve\n\nSteps:\n1. Analyze current state (Claude, standard gate)\n2. Generate plan (Claude, standard gate)\n3. Execute changes (Claude, strict gate)\n4. Validate changes (programmatic + Claude)\n5. Iterate if quality threshold not met (retry loop)\n","numLines":216,"startLine":1,"totalLines":216}}}

Step Mapping Engine (FR-024)\n\n### Mapping Types\n\nThe step mapping engine transforms source steps (from Phase 1 analysis) into generated steps (for code generation). Four mapping types are supported:\n\n| Mapping Type | Description | Justification Requirement |\n|-------------|-------------|--------------------------|\n| `1:1` | One source step maps to exactly one generated step | Optional — default mapping |\n| `1:N` | One source step splits into N generated steps | Required — explain split rationale |\n| `N:1` | N source steps merge into one generated step | Required — explain merge rationale |\n| `1:0` | One source step is eliminated | Required — must provide elimination record |\n\n### Mapping Algorithm\n\n```\nmap_source_to_generated(\n    source_steps: list[SourceStep],\n    classified_steps: list[ClassifiedStep],\n    dag: DependencyDAG,\n    gate_assignments: list[GateAssignment]\n) -> StepMappingResult\n```\n\n**Process**:\n1. For each source step `S-NNN`, determine the appropriate mapping type:\n   - If the step translates directly to one generated step → `1:1`\n   - If the step requires splitting (e.g., a batch operation with pre-batch and post-batch logic) → `1:N`\n   - If multiple source steps share enough implementation that they should be a single generated step → `N:1`\n   - If the step has no generated equivalent (e.g., absorbed into executor logic or eliminated) → `1:0`\n2. Assign generated step IDs in format `G-NNN` (sequential, zero-padded to 3 digits)\n3. Record justification for all non-1:1 mappings\n4. For `1:0` mappings, create an elimination record\n\n### Generated Step ID Assignment\n\n```\nassign_generated_ids(mappings: list[StepMapping]) -> list[StepMapping]\n```\n\nGenerated IDs are assigned sequentially based on the topological order of their source steps:\n- `G-001`, `G-002`, ..., `G-NNN`\n- For `1:N` splits, sub-IDs use the pattern `G-NNN` (each gets its own top-level ID)\n- For `N:1` merges, the merged step gets a single `G-NNN` ID\n- `1:0` eliminated steps receive no generated ID\n\n### Mapping Record Structure\n\n```yaml\nstep_mapping:\n  - source_id: \"S-001\"           # Source step from Phase 1\n    generated_step_ids: [\"G-001\"] # Generated step(s)\n    mapping_type: \"1:1\"          # Mapping type\n    justification: null          # Not required for 1:1\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Elimination Records (FR-025)\n\n### Record Structure\n\nSteps mapped as `1:0` must have an elimination record with all three required fields:\n\n```yaml\nelimination_records:\n  - source_id: \"S-NNN\"          # Which source step was eliminated\n    reason: \"<explanation>\"      # Why it was eliminated\n    approved_by: \"auto\" | \"user\" # Who approved the elimination\n```\n\n**Field requirements**:\n- `source_id`: Must reference a valid source step ID from Phase 1 analysis (non-empty string matching `S-\\d{3}`)\n- `reason`: Must be a non-empty string explaining why this step has no generated equivalent\n- `approved_by`: Must be either `\"auto\"` (if the elimination is self-evident, e.g., step absorbed into executor overhead) or `\"user\"` (if the elimination required user review)\n\n### Auto-Approval Criteria\n\nAn elimination may be auto-approved (`approved_by: \"auto\"`) when:\n- The step's function is absorbed into the executor's built-in behavior (e.g., step sequencing, retry logic)\n- The step is purely orchestrational with no domain-specific output\n- The step's output is a subset of another step's output (deduplication)\n\nAll other eliminations require `approved_by: \"user\"`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Coverage Invariant Enforcement (FR-025, FR-049)\n\n### Invariant Equation\n\n```\n|source_step_registry| == |mapped_steps| + |elimination_records|\n```\n\nWhere:\n- `|source_step_registry|` = number of source steps from Phase 1 (the `source_step_count` from D-0017)\n- `|mapped_steps|` = number of unique source steps that have at least one generated step mapping (mapping types 1:1, 1:N, or participating in N:1)\n- `|elimination_records|` = number of `1:0` elimination records\n\n### Enforcement Algorithm\n\n```\nenforce_coverage_invariant(\n    source_steps: list[SourceStep],\n    mappings: list[StepMapping],\n    eliminations: list[EliminationRecord]\n) -> CoverageInvariantResult\n```\n\n1. Compute `source_count = len(source_steps)`\n2. Compute `mapped_source_ids = set(m.source_id for m in mappings if m.mapping_type != \"1:0\")`\n3. Compute `eliminated_source_ids = set(e.source_id for e in eliminations)`\n4. Verify no overlap: `mapped_source_ids & eliminated_source_ids == {}`\n5. Verify completeness: `mapped_source_ids | eliminated_source_ids == {s.source_id for s in source_steps}`\n6. Verify count: `len(mapped_source_ids) + len(eliminated_source_ids) == source_count`\n\n**On violation**: The engine halts with a blocking error:\n```\nCOVERAGE_INVARIANT_VIOLATION: Source step count (N) != mapped (M) + eliminated (E)\nMissing source steps: [S-NNN, ...]\nDuplicate mappings: [S-NNN, ...]\nAction: Every source step must appear in exactly one mapping or elimination record.\n```\n\n### Result Structure\n\n```yaml\ncoverage_invariant:\n  source_step_count: 6           # |source_step_registry|\n  mapped_step_count: 6           # |mapped_steps|\n  eliminated_count: 0            # |elimination_records|\n  invariant_holds: true          # source == mapped + eliminated\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Test Execution: sc-cleanup-audit-protocol\n\n### Source Step Registry (from D-0017)\n\n| source_id | Name | Classification |\n|-----------|------|---------------|\n| S-001 | Discover and classify files | pure_programmatic |\n| S-002 | Surface scan (Pass 1) — batch | claude_assisted |\n| S-003 | Structural analysis (Pass 2) — batch | claude_assisted |\n| S-004 | Cross-cutting comparison (Pass 3) | claude_assisted |\n| S-005 | Consolidate findings | claude_assisted |\n| S-006 | Validate claims (spot-check) | claude_assisted |\n\n### Step Mapping Result\n\n| source_id | generated_step_ids | mapping_type | justification |\n|-----------|-------------------|-------------|---------------|\n| S-001 | [\"G-001\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-002 | [\"G-002\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-003 | [\"G-003\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-004 | [\"G-004\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-005 | [\"G-005\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-006 | [\"G-006\"] | 1:1 | null |\n\n**Mapping rationale**: The sc-cleanup-audit workflow has 6 well-defined steps with clear boundaries. Each source step maps directly to one generated step with no splits, merges, or eliminations needed. The batch operations (S-002, S-003) are handled within their respective generated steps using the executor's batch dispatch mechanism rather than splitting into separate steps.\n\n### Elimination Records\n\n```yaml\nelimination_records: []\n```\n\nNo steps eliminated — all 6 source steps have direct generated equivalents.\n\n### Coverage Invariant Verification\n\n```yaml\ncoverage_invariant:\n  source_step_count: 6\n  mapped_step_count: 6\n  eliminated_count: 0\n  invariant_holds: true    # 6 == 6 + 0\n```\n\n**Verification**:\n- `source_count = 6` (from D-0017)\n- `mapped_source_ids = {S-001, S-002, S-003, S-004, S-005, S-006}` → count = 6\n- `eliminated_source_ids = {}` → count = 0\n- No overlap: `{} & {S-001..S-006} == {}` ✅\n- Completeness: `{S-001..S-006} | {} == {S-001..S-006}` ✅\n- Count: `6 + 0 == 6` ✅\n\n**Coverage invariant HOLDS** ✅\n\n---\n\n## 5. Acceptance Criteria Verification\n\n| Criterion | Status |\n|-----------|--------|\n| Step mapping engine correctly records all 4 mapping types (1:1, 1:N, N:1, 1:0) with justifications | ✅ PASS — all types defined with justification requirements |\n| Coverage invariant `\\|source_step_registry\\| == \\|mapped_steps\\| + \\|elimination_records\\|` verified for test workflow | ✅ PASS — 6 == 6 + 0 |\n| All elimination records contain non-empty source_id, reason, and approved_by fields | ✅ PASS — no eliminations in test workflow; field requirements specified |\n| Step mapping specification documented in D-0022/spec.md | ✅ PASS — this document |\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3914,"cache_read_input_tokens":105523,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":3914,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":25,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"392951ff-641a-4718-a34a-e7e268437669","uuid":"dd1c6d0f-eeb2-413a-8486-fc6602918a5e"}

Elimination Records (FR-025)\n\n### Record Structure\n\nSteps mapped as `1:0` must have an elimination record with all three required fields:\n\n```yaml\nelimination_records:\n  - source_id: \"S-NNN\"          # Which source step was eliminated\n    reason: \"<explanation>\"      # Why it was eliminated\n    approved_by: \"auto\" | \"user\" # Who approved the elimination\n```\n\n**Field requirements**:\n- `source_id`: Must reference a valid source step ID from Phase 1 analysis (non-empty string matching `S-\\d{3}`)\n- `reason`: Must be a non-empty string explaining why this step has no generated equivalent\n- `approved_by`: Must be either `\"auto\"` (if the elimination is self-evident, e.g., step absorbed into executor overhead) or `\"user\"` (if the elimination required user review)\n\n### Auto-Approval Criteria\n\nAn elimination may be auto-approved (`approved_by: \"auto\"`) when:\n- The step's function is absorbed into the executor's built-in behavior (e.g., step sequencing, retry logic)\n- The step is purely orchestrational with no domain-specific output\n- The step's output is a subset of another step's output (deduplication)\n\nAll other eliminations require `approved_by: \"user\"`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Coverage Invariant Enforcement (FR-025, FR-049)\n\n### Invariant Equation\n\n```\n|source_step_registry| == |mapped_steps| + |elimination_records|\n```\n\nWhere:\n- `|source_step_registry|` = number of source steps from Phase 1 (the `source_step_count` from D-0017)\n- `|mapped_steps|` = number of unique source steps that have at least one generated step mapping (mapping types 1:1, 1:N, or participating in N:1)\n- `|elimination_records|` = number of `1:0` elimination records\n\n### Enforcement Algorithm\n\n```\nenforce_coverage_invariant(\n    source_steps: list[SourceStep],\n    mappings: list[StepMapping],\n    eliminations: list[EliminationRecord]\n) -> CoverageInvariantResult\n```\n\n1. Compute `source_count = len(source_steps)`\n2. Compute `mapped_source_ids = set(m.source_id for m in mappings if m.mapping_type != \"1:0\")`\n3. Compute `eliminated_source_ids = set(e.source_id for e in eliminations)`\n4. Verify no overlap: `mapped_source_ids & eliminated_source_ids == {}`\n5. Verify completeness: `mapped_source_ids | eliminated_source_ids == {s.source_id for s in source_steps}`\n6. Verify count: `len(mapped_source_ids) + len(eliminated_source_ids) == source_count`\n\n**On violation**: The engine halts with a blocking error:\n```\nCOVERAGE_INVARIANT_VIOLATION: Source step count (N) != mapped (M) + eliminated (E)\nMissing source steps: [S-NNN, ...]\nDuplicate mappings: [S-NNN, ...]\nAction: Every source step must appear in exactly one mapping or elimination record.\n```\n\n### Result Structure\n\n```yaml\ncoverage_invariant:\n  source_step_count: 6           # |source_step_registry|\n  mapped_step_count: 6           # |mapped_steps|\n  eliminated_count: 0            # |elimination_records|\n  invariant_holds: true          # source == mapped + eliminated\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Test Execution: sc-cleanup-audit-protocol\n\n### Source Step Registry (from D-0017)\n\n| source_id | Name | Classification |\n|-----------|------|---------------|\n| S-001 | Discover and classify files | pure_programmatic |\n| S-002 | Surface scan (Pass 1) — batch | claude_assisted |\n| S-003 | Structural analysis (Pass 2) — batch | claude_assisted |\n| S-004 | Cross-cutting comparison (Pass 3) | claude_assisted |\n| S-005 | Consolidate findings | claude_assisted |\n| S-006 | Validate claims (spot-check) | claude_assisted |\n\n### Step Mapping Result\n\n| source_id | generated_step_ids | mapping_type | justification |\n|-----------|-------------------|-------------|---------------|\n| S-001 | [\"G-001\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-002 | [\"G-002\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-003 | [\"G-003\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-004 | [\"G-004\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-005 | [\"G-005\"] | 1:1 | null |\n| S-006 | [\"G-006\"] | 1:1 | null |\n\n**Mapping rationale**: The sc-cleanup-audit workflow has 6 well-defined steps with clear boundaries. Each source step maps directly to one generated step with no splits, merges, or eliminations needed. The batch operations (S-002, S-003) are handled within their respective generated steps using the executor's batch dispatch mechanism rather than splitting into separate steps.\n\n### Elimination Records\n\n```yaml\nelimination_records: []\n```\n\nNo steps eliminated — all 6 source steps have direct generated equivalents.\n\n### Coverage Invariant Verification\n\n```yaml\ncoverage_invariant:\n  source_step_count: 6\n  mapped_step_count: 6\n  eliminated_count: 0\n  invariant_holds: true    # 6 == 6 + 0\n```\n\n**Verification**:\n- `source_count = 6` (from D-0017)\n- `mapped_source_ids = {S-001, S-002, S-003, S-004, S-005, S-006}` → count = 6\n- `eliminated_source_ids = {}` → count = 0\n- No overlap: `{} & {S-001..S-006} == {}` ✅\n- Completeness: `{S-001..S-006} | {} == {S-001..S-006}` ✅\n- Count: `6 + 0 == 6` ✅\n\n**Coverage invariant HOLDS** ✅\n\n---\n\n## 5. Acceptance Criteria Verification\n\n| Criterion | Status |\n|-----------|--------|\n| Step mapping engine correctly records all 4 mapping types (1:1, 1:N, N:1, 1:0) with justifications | ✅ PASS — all types defined with justification requirements |\n| Coverage invariant `\\|source_step_registry\\| == \\|mapped_steps\\| + \\|elimination_records\\|` verified for test workflow | ✅ PASS — 6 == 6 + 0 |\n| All elimination records contain non-empty source_id, reason, and approved_by fields | ✅ PASS — no eliminations in test workflow; field requirements specified |\n| Step mapping specification documented in D-0022/spec.md | ✅ PASS — this document |\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

This ref provides the detailed specification patterns for converting a workflow analysis into concrete code designs.\n     4→\n     5→## Step Graph Design\n     6→\n     7→### Step Definition Pattern\n     8→\n     9→Every workflow operation that produces an artifact maps to a `Step`:\n    10→\n    11→```python\n    12→Step(\n    13→    id=\"step-id\",              # kebab-case, unique within pipeline\n    14→    prompt=build_X_prompt(),   # Function from prompts.py\n    15→    output_file=\"artifact.md\", # Relative to work_dir\n    16→    gate=STEP_GATE,            # From gates.py\n    17→    gate_mode=GateMode.BLOCKING,  # BLOCKING (default) or TRAILING\n    18→    timeout_seconds=600,       # Per-step timeout\n    19→    inputs=[\"dep1.md\"],        # Files this step reads\n    20→    retry_limit=1,             # How many retries on gate failure\n    21→    model=None,                # None = use default from config\n    22→)\n    23→```\n    24→\n    25→### Gate Mode Selection\n    26→\n    27→Choose `GateMode` based on step criticality:\n    28→- `BLOCKING` (default): Pipeline halts if gate fails. Use for steps whose output is consumed by downstream steps.\n    29→- `TRAILING`: Gate evaluates asynchronously; pipeline continues. passes their gate\n    56→\n    57→## Model Design Patterns\n    58→\n    59→### Config Model\n    60→\n    61→Always extend `PipelineConfig`:\n    62→\n    63→```python\n    64→@dataclass\n 81→```\n    82→\n    83→### Status Enum\n    84→\n    85→Sprint-style pipelines need richer status than generic `StepStatus`:\n    86→\n    87→```python\n    88→class StepPhaseStatus(Enum):\n    89→    PENDING = \"pending\"\n    90→    RUNNING = \"running\"\n    91→    PASS = \"pass\"\n    92→    PASS_NO_SIGNAL = \"pass_no_signal\"    # Completed but no structured report\n    93→    PASS_NO_REPORT optional/informational steps)\n   143→EXEMPT_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   144→    required_frontmatter_fields=[],\n   145→    min_lines=0,\n   146→    enforcement_tier=\"EXEMPT\",\n   147→)\n   148→\n   149→# Light: file exists and non-empty\n   150→LIGHT_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   151→    required_frontmatter_fields=[],\n   152→    min_lines=0,\n   153→    enforcement_tier=\"LIGHT\",\n   154→)\n   155→\n   156→# Standard: structural validation\n   157→STANDARD_GATE = GateCriteria(\n   158→    required_frontmatter_fields=[\"title\", \"status\"],\n   159→    min_lines=50,\n   160→       name=\"refs_resolve\",\n   176→            check_fn=_cross_refs_resolve,\n   177→            failure_message=\"Cross-references do not resolve to valid targets\",\n   178→        ),\n   179→    ],\n   180→)\n   181→```\n   182→\n   183→### Semantic Check Functions\n   184→\n   185→Semantic checks are pure functions matching the `Callable[[str], bool]` signature — they take file content and return a boolean:\n   186→\n   187→```python\n   188→def _no_heading_gaps(content: str) -> bool:\n   189→    \"\"\"Verify heading hierarchy has no gaps (H1->H3 without H2).\"\"\"\n   190→    # ... implementation ...\n   191→    return True  # or False on failure\n   192→\n   193→def _has_required_sections(content: str) -> bool:\n   194→    \"\"\"Verify all required sections are present.\"\"\"\n   195→    required = {\"## Summary\", \"## Findings\", \"## Recommendations\"}\n   196→    present = {line.strip() for line in content.splitlines() if line.startswith(\"## \")}\n   197→    missing = Steps that produce markdown with frontmatter get automatic validation:\n   204→\n   205→```yaml\n   206→---\n   207→title: Diff Analysis\n   208→status: complete\n   209→diff_points: 12\n   210→convergence_ready: true\n   211→---\n   212→```\n   213→\n   214→## Prompt Design Patterns\n   215→\n   216→### Prompt Builder Structure\n   217→\n   218→Each step's prompt is a function that takes inputs and returns a complete prompt string:\n   219→\n   220→```python\n   221→def build_analysis_prompt(source_path: Path, config: MyConfig) -> str:\n   222→    return f\"\"\"Read the source file and produce a structured analysis.\n   223→\n   224→Source: {source_path}\n   225→Depth: {config.depth}\n   226→\n   227→## Required Output Format\n   228→\n   229→Write your analysis to the output file with this structure:\n   230→\n   231→```yaml\n   232→---\n   233→title: Analysis Report\n   234→status: complete\n   235→finding_count: <integer>\n   236→---\n   237→```\n   238→\n   239→## Sections Required\n   240→\n   241→### Summary\n   242→Brief overview of findings.\n   243→\n   244→### Findings\n   245→Numbered list of findings with evidence.\n   246→\n   247→### Recommendations\n   248→Actionable next steps.\n   249→\n   250→## Machine-Readable Markers\n   251→\n   252→At the end of your output, include:\n   253→```\n   254→EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE\n   255→```\n   256→or\n   257→```\n   258→EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: HALT\n   259→```\n   260→\"\"\"\n   261→```\n   262→\n   263→### Key Prompt Rules\n   264→\n   265→1. **Specify output file format** — Tell Claude exactly what frontmatter fields to include\n   266→2. **Require machine-readable markers** — `EXIT_RECOMMENDATION: CONTINUE|HALT` for status determination\n   267→3. **Embed input content when small** — Under ~50KB, embed directly in prompt; otherwise use `--file` args\n   268→4. **Be explicit about sections** — Name every required section; don't leave structure to inference\n   269→5. **Include depth/focus constraints** — If the step has configurable depth, encode it in the prompt\n   270→\n   271→### Input Embedding Pattern\n   272→\n   273→```python\n   274→def _embed_inputs(prompt: str, inputs: list[Path], config: MyConfig) -> tuple[str, list[str]]:\n   275→    \"\"\"Embed small input files directly into prompt, return file args for large ones.\"\"\"\n   276→    file_args = []\n   277→    for input_path in inputs:\n   278→        full_path = config.work_dir / input_path\n   279→        if full_path.stat().st_size < 50_000:\n   280→            content = full_path.read_text()\n   281→            prompt += f\"\\n\\n---\\n## Input: {input_path}\\n\\n{content}\"\n   282→        else:\n   283→            file_args.append(str(full_path))\n   284→    return prompt, file_args\n   285→```\n   286→\n   287→## Executor Design Patterns\n   288→\n   289→### Sprint-Style Supervisor Loop\n   290→\n   291→The sprint executor pattern provides supervised execution with monitoring. IMPORTANT: Sprint uses synchronous execution with `threading` for parallelism, NOT `async/await`. Use `time.sleep()` polling loops and `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` for batch dispatch.\n   292→\n   293→```python\n   294→def execute_pipeline(config: MyConfig) -> MyResult:\n   295→    # 1. Pre-flight checks\n   296→    verify_claude_binary()\n   297→\n   298→    # 2. Setup infrastructure\n   299→    signal_handler = SignalHandler()\n   300→    logger = MyLogger(config)\n   301→    tui = MyTUI(config)\n   302→    monitor = OutputMonitor()\n   303→    result = MyResult(config=config)\n   304→    ledger = TurnLedger(initial_budget=config.max_turns)\n   305→\n   306→    # 3. Start TUI\n   307→    tui.start()\n   308→\n   309→    try:\n   310→        for step in config.steps:\n   311→            if signal_handler.shutdown_requested:\n   312→                break\n   313→\n   314→            # 4. Reset monitor for this step\n   315→            monitor.reset(config.output_file(step))\n   316→            monitor.start()\n   317→\n   318→            # 5. Launch Claude subprocess\n   319→            process = ClaudeProcess(config, step)\n   320→            process.start()\n   321→\n   322→            # 6. Supervision loop\n   323→            while process.is_running():\n   324→                if signal_handler.shutdown_requested:\n   325→                    process.stop()\n   326→                    break\n   327→\n   328→                state = monitor.get_state()\n   329→\n   330→                # Stall detection\n   331→                if state.stall_seconds > config.stall_timeout:\n   332→                    process.stop()\n   333→                    break\n   334→\n   335→                # TUI update\n   336→                tui.update(step, state)\n   337→                time.sleep(0.5)\n   338→\n   339→            # 7.                     if r.status in (MyStatus.PENDING, MyStatus.INCOMPLETE))\n   537→        return remaining_steps * 25  # Default allocation per step\n   538→```\n   539→\n   540→## Pure-Programmatic Step Execution\n   541→\n   542→Not all steps need Claude.
